<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Circulatory system</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Organ system for circulating blood in animals</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the animal circulatory system. For plants, see <a href="/wiki/Vascular_tissue" title="Vascular tissue">Vascular tissue</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Several terms redirect here. For the song by Ed Sheeran, see <a href="/wiki/Bloodstream_(song)" title="Bloodstream (song)">Bloodstream (song)</a>. For the album by Youves, see <a href="/wiki/Cardio-Vascular" title="Cardio-Vascular">Cardio-Vascular</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-above" colspan="2" style="background-color:dimgray; color: white">Circulatory system</th></tr><tr><td class="infobox-image" colspan="2"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Circulatory_System_en.svg"><img alt="Circulatory System en.svg" data-file-height="830" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="377" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Circulatory_System_en.svg/250px-Circulatory_System_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Circulatory_System_en.svg/375px-Circulatory_System_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Circulatory_System_en.svg/500px-Circulatory_System_en.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a><div class="infobox-caption">The human circulatory system (simplified). Red indicates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxygenated_blood" title="Oxygenated blood">oxygenated blood</a> carried in <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">arteries</a>. Blue indicates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deoxygenated_blood" title="Deoxygenated blood">deoxygenated blood</a> carried in <a href="/wiki/Vein" title="Vein">veins</a>. <a href="/wiki/Capillary" title="Capillary">Capillaries</a> join the arteries and veins.</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-header" colspan="2" style="background-color: #efefef">Identifiers</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-right:0.25em"><a href="/wiki/Medical_Subject_Headings" title="Medical Subject Headings">MeSH</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="external text" href="https://meshb.nlm.nih.gov/record/ui?ui=D002319" rel="nofollow">D002319</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-right:0.25em"><a href="/wiki/Terminologia_Anatomica" title="Terminologia Anatomica">TA98</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="external text" href="http://www.unifr.ch/ifaa/Public/EntryPage/TA98%20Tree/Entity%20TA98%20EN/12.0.00.000%20Entity%20TA98%20EN.htm" rel="nofollow">A12.0.00.000</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-right:0.25em"><a href="/wiki/Terminologia_Anatomica" title="Terminologia Anatomica">TA2</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="external text" href="https://ta2viewer.openanatomy.org/?id=3891" rel="nofollow">3891</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-right:0.25em"><a href="/wiki/Foundational_Model_of_Anatomy" title="Foundational Model of Anatomy">FMA</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="external text" href="https://bioportal.bioontology.org/ontologies/FMA/?p=classes&amp;conceptid=http%3A%2F%2Fpurl.org%2Fsig%2Font%2Ffma%2Ffma7161" rel="nofollow">7161</a></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-below" colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Anatomical_terminology" title="Anatomical terminology">Anatomical terminology</a><div style="text-align: right;"><small class="noprint">[<a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q11068" title="d:Q11068">edit on Wikidata</a>]</small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The blood <b>circulatory system</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Organ_system" title="Organ system">system of organs</a> that includes the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blood_vessel" title="Blood vessel">blood vessels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blood" title="Blood">blood</a> which is circulated throughout the entire body of a human or other vertebrate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hall-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saladin2_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saladin2-2">[2]</a></sup> It includes the <b>cardiovascular system</b>, or <b>vascular system</b>, that consists of the heart and blood vessels (from Greek <i>kardia</i> meaning <i>heart</i>, and from Latin <i>vascula</i> meaning <i>vessels</i>). The circulatory system has two divisions, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systemic_circulation" title="Systemic circulation">systemic circulation or circuit</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation or circuit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saladin3_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saladin3-3">[3]</a></sup> Some sources use the terms <i>cardiovascular system</i> and <i>vascular system</i> interchangeably with the <i>circulatory system</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncbibooks_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncbibooks-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>The network of blood vessels are the <a href="/wiki/Great_vessels" title="Great vessels">great vessels</a> of the heart including large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elastic_arteries" title="Elastic arteries">elastic arteries</a>, and large <a href="/wiki/Vein" title="Vein">veins</a>; other arteries, smaller <a href="/wiki/Arteriole" title="Arteriole">arterioles</a>, 
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capillaries" title="Capillaries">capillaries</a> that join with <a href="/wiki/Venule" title="Venule">venules</a> (small veins), and other veins. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Closed_circulatory_system" title="Closed circulatory system">circulatory system is closed</a> in vertebrates, which means that the blood never leaves the network of blood vessels. Some <a href="/wiki/Invertebrate" title="Invertebrate">invertebrates</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">arthropods</a> have an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_circulatory_system" title="Open circulatory system">open circulatory system</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diploblast" title="Diploblast">Diploblasts</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sponges" title="Sponges">sponges</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comb_jellies" title="Comb jellies">comb jellies</a> lack a circulatory system. 
</p><p>Blood is a <a href="/wiki/Body_fluid" title="Body fluid">fluid</a> consisting of <a href="/wiki/Blood_plasma" title="Blood plasma">plasma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_blood_cell" title="Red blood cell">red blood cells</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_blood_cell" title="White blood cell">white blood cells</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platelets" title="Platelets">platelets</a> that is circulated around the body carrying <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a> to the tissues, and <a href="/wiki/Metabolic_waste" title="Metabolic waste">waste materials</a> away. Circulated nutrients include <a href="/wiki/Protein_(nutrient)" title="Protein (nutrient)">proteins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mineral_(nutrient)" title="Mineral (nutrient)">minerals</a>, other components transported are <a href="/wiki/Gas" title="Gas">gases</a> such as oxygen, and  <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hormone" title="Hormone">hormones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hemoglobin" title="Hemoglobin">hemoglobin</a>;  providing nourishment, help in the <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a> to fight <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diseases" title="Diseases">diseases</a>, and in maintaining <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostasis</a> by <a href="/wiki/Thermoregulation" title="Thermoregulation">stabilizing temperature</a> and <a href="/wiki/PH#Living_systems" title="PH">natural pH</a>. 
</p><p>In vertebrates, complementary to the circulatory system is the <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_system" title="Lymphatic system">lymphatic system</a>. This system carries excess plasma <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capillary_filtration" title="Capillary filtration">filtered</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capillaries" title="Capillaries">capillaries</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstitial_fluid" title="Interstitial fluid">interstitial fluid</a> between cells, away from the body tissues in an accessory route to return the excess fluid back to the blood circulation as <a href="/wiki/Lymph" title="Lymph">lymph</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sherwood,_Lauralee_2011_401_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sherwood,_Lauralee_2011_401-5">[5]</a></sup>  The passage of lymph takes much longer than that of blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRU_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-CRU-6">[6]</a></sup> The lymphatic system is a subsystem that is essential for the functioning of the blood circulatory system; without it the blood would become depleted of fluid. The lymphatic system works together with the <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saladin4_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saladin4-7">[7]</a></sup> Unlike the  closed circulatory system, the lymphatic system is an open system. Some sources describe it as a <i>secondary circulatory system</i>.  
</p><p>The circulatory system can be affected by many <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular diseases</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiologist" title="Cardiologist">Cardiologists</a> are medical professionals which specialise in the heart, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiothoracic_surgeon" title="Cardiothoracic surgeon">cardiothoracic surgeons</a> specialise in operating on the heart and its surrounding areas. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vascular_surgeon" title="Vascular surgeon">Vascular surgeons</a> focus on disorders of the blood vessels, and lymphatic vessels.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span></h2>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Human_cardiovascular_system"></span>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1317" data-file-width="1942" decoding="async" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg/350px-2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg/525px-2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg/700px-2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2101_Blood_Flow_Through_the_Heart.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Blood flow in the pulmonary and systemic circulations showing capillary networks in the torso sections</div></div></div>
<p>The circulatory system includes the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blood_vessel" title="Blood vessel">blood vessels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blood" title="Blood">blood</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saladin2_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Saladin2-2">[2]</a></sup> The <b>cardiovascular system</b> in all vertebrates, consists of the heart and blood vessels. The circulatory system is further divided into two major circuits – a <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a>, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systemic_circulation" title="Systemic circulation">systemic circulation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hall_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hall-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saladin3_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Saladin3-3">[3]</a></sup> The pulmonary circulation is a circuit loop from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right_heart" title="Right heart">right heart</a> taking deoxygenated blood to the <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">lungs</a> where it is oxygenated and returned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_heart" title="Left heart">left heart</a>. The systemic circulation is a circuit loop that delivers oxygenated blood from the left heart to the rest of the body, and returns deoxygenated blood back to the right heart via <a href="/wiki/Great_vessels" title="Great vessels">large veins</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Venae_cavae" title="Venae cavae">venae cavae</a>. The systemic circulation can also be defined as two parts – a <i>macrocirculation</i> and a <i><a href="/wiki/Microcirculation" title="Microcirculation">microcirculation</a></i>. An average adult contains five to six quarts (roughly 4.7 to 5.7 liters) of blood, accounting for approximately 7% of their total body weight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Blood consists of <a href="/wiki/Blood_plasma" title="Blood plasma">plasma</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_blood_cells" title="Red blood cells">red blood cells</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_blood_cells" title="White blood cells">white blood cells</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Platelets" title="Platelets">platelets</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digestive_system" title="Digestive system">digestive system</a> also works with the circulatory system to provide the nutrients the system needs to keep the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a> pumping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guyton_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guyton-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Further circulatory routes are associated, such as the <a href="/wiki/Coronary_circulation" title="Coronary circulation">coronary circulation</a> to the heart itself, the <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_circulation" title="Cerebral circulation">cerebral circulation</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">brain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renal_circulation" title="Renal circulation">renal circulation</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Kidney" title="Kidney">kidneys</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_circulation" title="Bronchial circulation">bronchial circulation</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronchi" title="Bronchi">bronchi</a> in the lungs.
</p><p>The human circulatory system is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Closed_circulatory_system" title="Closed circulatory system">closed</a>, meaning that the blood is contained within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blood_vessels" title="Blood vessels">vascular network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawton_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lawton-11">[11]</a></sup> Nutrients travel through tiny blood vessels of the microcirculation to reach organs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawton_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lawton-11">[11]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_system" title="Lymphatic system">lymphatic system</a> is an essential subsystem of the circulatory system consisting of a network of <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_vessel" title="Lymphatic vessel">lymphatic vessels</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lymph_nodes" title="Lymph nodes">lymph nodes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lymphatic_organs" title="Lymphatic organs">organs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lymphatic_tissues" title="Lymphatic tissues">tissues</a> and circulating <a href="/wiki/Lymph" title="Lymph">lymph</a>. This subsystem is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_circulatory_system" title="Open circulatory system">open system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gartner_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gartner-12">[12]</a></sup> A major function is to carry the lymph, draining and returning <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstitial_fluid" title="Interstitial fluid">interstitial fluid</a> into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lymphatic_duct" title="Lymphatic duct">lymphatic ducts</a> back to the heart for return to the circulatory system. Another <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_system#Function" title="Lymphatic system">major function</a> is working together with the <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a> to provide defense against <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">pathogens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alberts_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Alberts-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heart">Heart</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">Heart</a></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg/220px-Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg/330px-Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg/440px-Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blood_oxygenation_to_the_pulmonary_and_systemic_circulation.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Diagram of the human <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a> showing blood oxygenation to the pulmonary and systemic circulation</div></div></div></div>
<p>The heart pumps blood to all parts of the body providing <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> to every <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cell</a>, and removing waste products. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_heart" title="Left heart">left heart</a> pumps oxygenated blood returned from the lungs to the rest of the body in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systemic_circulation" title="Systemic circulation">systemic circulation</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right_heart" title="Right heart">right heart</a> pumps deoxygenated blood to the lungs in the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a>. In the human <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a> there is one <a href="/wiki/Atrium_(heart)" title="Atrium (heart)">atrium</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Ventricle_(heart)" title="Ventricle (heart)">ventricle</a> for each circulation, and with both a systemic and a pulmonary circulation there are four chambers in total: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_atrium" title="Left atrium">left atrium</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_ventricle" title="Left ventricle">left ventricle</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right_atrium" title="Right atrium">right atrium</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right_ventricle" title="Right ventricle">right ventricle</a>. The right atrium is the upper chamber of the right side of the heart. The blood that is returned to the right atrium is deoxygenated (poor in oxygen) and passed into the right ventricle to be pumped through the pulmonary artery to the lungs for re-oxygenation and removal of carbon dioxide. The left atrium receives newly oxygenated blood from the lungs as well as the pulmonary vein which is passed into the strong left ventricle to be pumped through the aorta to the different organs of the body.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pulmonary_circulation">Pulmonary circulation</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">Pulmonary circulation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="868" data-file-width="1507" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg/370px-2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg/555px-2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg/740px-2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg 2x" width="370"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2119_Pulmonary_Circuit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a> as it passes from the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>. Showing both the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_artery" title="Pulmonary artery">pulmonary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_artery" title="Bronchial artery">bronchial arteries</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a> is the portion of the cardiovascular system in which <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a>-depleted blood is pumped away from the heart, via the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_artery" title="Pulmonary artery">pulmonary artery</a>, to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lungs" title="Lungs">lungs</a> and returned, oxygenated, to the heart via the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_vein" title="Pulmonary vein">pulmonary vein</a>.
</p><p>Oxygen-deprived blood from the superior and inferior <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vena_cava" title="Vena cava">vena cava</a> enters the right atrium of the heart and flows through the <a href="/wiki/Tricuspid_valve" title="Tricuspid valve">tricuspid valve</a> (right atrioventricular valve) into the right ventricle, from which it is then pumped through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulmonary_semilunar_valve" title="Pulmonary semilunar valve">pulmonary semilunar valve</a> into the pulmonary artery to the lungs. <a href="/wiki/Gas_exchange" title="Gas exchange">Gas exchange</a> occurs in the lungs, whereby <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub></a> is released from the blood, and oxygen is absorbed. The pulmonary vein returns the now oxygen-rich blood to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_atrium" title="Left atrium">left atrium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guyton_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guyton-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>A separate system known as the <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_circulation" title="Bronchial circulation">bronchial circulation</a> supplies blood to the tissue of the larger airways of the lung.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Systemic_circulation">Systemic circulation</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1099" data-file-width="1859" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg/310px-2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg/465px-2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg/620px-2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2105_Capillary_Bed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Capillary bed</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capillary_system_CERT.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="525" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Capillary_system_CERT.jpg/220px-Capillary_system_CERT.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Capillary_system_CERT.jpg/330px-Capillary_system_CERT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Capillary_system_CERT.jpg/440px-Capillary_system_CERT.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capillary_system_CERT.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Diagram of capillary network joining the arterial system with the venous system.</div></div></div>
<p>The systemic circulation is a circuit loop that delivers oxygenated blood from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_heart" title="Left heart">left heart</a> to the rest of the body through the <a href="/wiki/Aorta" title="Aorta">aorta</a>. Deoxygenated blood is returned in the systemic circulation to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right_heart" title="Right heart">right heart</a> via two large veins, the <a href="/wiki/Inferior_vena_cava" title="Inferior vena cava">inferior vena cava</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Superior_vena_cava" title="Superior vena cava">superior vena cava</a>, where it is pumped from the right atrium into the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a> for oxygenation. The systemic circulation can also be defined as having two parts – a macrocirculation and a <a href="/wiki/Microcirculation" title="Microcirculation">microcirculation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guyton_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Guyton-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blood_vessels">Blood vessels</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Blood_vessel" title="Blood vessel">blood vessels</a> of the circulatory system are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arteries" title="Arteries">arteries</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veins" title="Veins">veins</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capillaries" title="Capillaries">capillaries</a>. The large arteries and veins that take blood to, and away from the heart are known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_vessels" title="Great vessels">great vessels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray's_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray's-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arteries">Arteries</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">Artery</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Arterial_tree" title="Arterial tree">Arterial tree</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vein_art_near.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Vein_art_near.png/220px-Vein_art_near.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Vein_art_near.png/330px-Vein_art_near.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Vein_art_near.png/440px-Vein_art_near.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vein_art_near.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depiction of the heart, major veins and arteries constructed from body scans</div></div></div>
<p>Oxygenated blood enters the systemic circulation when leaving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_ventricle" title="Left ventricle">left ventricle</a>, through the <a href="/wiki/Aortic_valve" title="Aortic valve">aortic semilunar valve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iaizzo_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Iaizzo-15">[15]</a></sup> The first part of the systemic circulation is the <a href="/wiki/Aorta" title="Aorta">aorta</a>, a massive and thick-walled artery. The aorta arches and gives branches supplying the upper part of the body after passing through the aortic opening of the diaphragm at the level of thoracic ten vertebra, it enters the abdomen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iaizzo_two_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Iaizzo_two-16">[16]</a></sup> Later, it descends down and supplies branches to abdomen, pelvis, perineum and the lower limbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Iaizzo_three_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Iaizzo_three-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>The walls of the aorta are elastic. This elasticity helps to maintain the <a href="/wiki/Blood_pressure" title="Blood pressure">blood pressure</a> throughout the body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vaz_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vaz-18">[18]</a></sup> When the aorta receives almost five litres of blood from the heart, it recoils and is responsible for pulsating blood pressure. As the aorta branches into smaller arteries, their elasticity goes on decreasing and their compliance goes on increasing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vaz_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vaz-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Capillaries">Capillaries</span></h4>
<p>Arteries branch into small passages called <a href="/wiki/Arteriole" title="Arteriole">arterioles</a> and then into the <a href="/wiki/Capillary" title="Capillary">capillaries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The capillaries merge to bring blood into the venous system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Veins">Veins</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vein" title="Vein">Vein</a></div>
<p>Capillaries merge into <a href="/wiki/Venule" title="Venule">venules</a>, which merge into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veins" title="Veins">veins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mcconnell_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mcconnell-21">[21]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venous_system" title="Venous system">venous system</a> feeds into the two major veins: the <a href="/wiki/Superior_vena_cava" title="Superior vena cava">superior vena cava</a> – which mainly drains tissues above the heart – and the <a href="/wiki/Inferior_vena_cava" title="Inferior vena cava">inferior vena cava</a> – which mainly drains tissues below the heart. These two large veins empty into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right_atrium" title="Right atrium">right atrium</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floyd_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Floyd-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portal_veins">Portal veins</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portal_venous_system" title="Portal venous system">Portal venous system</a></div>
<p>The general rule is that arteries from the heart branch out into capillaries, which collect into veins leading back to the heart. <a href="/wiki/Portal_venous_system" title="Portal venous system">Portal veins</a> are a slight exception to this. In humans the only significant example is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hepatic_portal_vein" title="Hepatic portal vein">hepatic portal vein</a> which combines from capillaries around the <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract" title="Gastrointestinal tract">gastrointestinal tract</a> where the blood absorbs the various products of digestion; rather than leading directly back to the heart, the hepatic portal vein branches into a second capillary system in the <a href="/wiki/Liver" title="Liver">liver</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coronary_circulation">Coronary circulation</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coronary_circulation" title="Coronary circulation">Coronary circulation</a></div>
<p>The heart itself is supplied with oxygen and nutrients through a small "loop" of the systemic circulation and derives very little from the blood contained within the four chambers.
The coronary circulation system provides a blood supply to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Myocardium" title="Myocardium">heart muscle</a> itself. The coronary circulation begins near the origin of the <a href="/wiki/Aorta" title="Aorta">aorta</a> by two <a href="/wiki/Coronary_arteries" title="Coronary arteries">coronary arteries</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Right_coronary_artery" title="Right coronary artery">right coronary artery</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Left_coronary_artery" title="Left coronary artery">left coronary artery</a>. After nourishing the heart muscle, blood returns through the coronary veins into the <a href="/wiki/Coronary_sinus" title="Coronary sinus">coronary sinus</a> and from this one into the right atrium. Back flow of blood through its opening during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atrial_systole" title="Atrial systole">atrial systole</a> is prevented by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thebesian_valve" title="Thebesian valve">Thebesian valve</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Smallest_cardiac_veins" title="Smallest cardiac veins">smallest cardiac veins</a> drain directly into the heart chambers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guyton_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-Guyton-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cerebral_circulation">Cerebral circulation</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_circulation" title="Cerebral circulation">Cerebral circulation</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brain" title="Brain">brain</a> has a dual blood supply, an <i>anterior</i> and a <i>posterior circulation</i> from arteries at its front and back. The anterior circulation arises from the <a href="/wiki/Internal_carotid_artery" title="Internal carotid artery">internal carotid arteries</a> to supply the front of the brain. The posterior circulation arises from the <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_artery" title="Vertebral artery">vertebral arteries</a>, to supply the back of the brain and <a href="/wiki/Brainstem" title="Brainstem">brainstem</a>. The circulation from the front and the back join (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anastomise" title="Anastomise">anastomise</a>) at the <a href="/wiki/Circle_of_Willis" title="Circle of Willis">circle of Willis</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renal_circulation">Renal circulation</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Renal_circulation" title="Renal circulation">renal circulation</a> is the blood supply to the <a href="/wiki/Kidney" title="Kidney">kidneys</a>, contains many specialized blood vessels and receives around 20% of the cardiac output. It branches from the <a href="/wiki/Abdominal_aorta" title="Abdominal aorta">abdominal aorta</a> and returns blood to the ascending <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vena_cava" title="Vena cava">vena cava</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Heart_development" title="Heart development">Heart development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasculogenesis" title="Vasculogenesis">Vasculogenesis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fetal_circulation" title="Fetal circulation">Fetal circulation</a></div>
<p>The development of the circulatory system starts with <a href="/wiki/Vasculogenesis" title="Vasculogenesis">vasculogenesis</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Embryo" title="Embryo">embryo</a>. The human arterial and venous systems develop from different areas in the embryo. The arterial system develops mainly from the <a href="/wiki/Aortic_arches" title="Aortic arches">aortic arches</a>, six pairs of arches that develop on the upper part of the embryo. The venous system arises from three bilateral veins during weeks 4 – 8 of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_embryogenesis" title="Human embryogenesis">embryogenesis</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fetal_circulation" title="Fetal circulation">Fetal circulation</a> begins within the 8th week of development. Fetal circulation does not include the lungs, which are bypassed via the <a href="/wiki/Truncus_arteriosus" title="Truncus arteriosus">truncus arteriosus</a>. Before birth the <a href="/wiki/Fetus" title="Fetus">fetus</a> obtains <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a>) from the mother through the <a href="/wiki/Placenta" title="Placenta">placenta</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Umbilical_cord" title="Umbilical cord">umbilical cord</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whitaker_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whitaker-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arteries_2">Arteries</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aortic_arches" title="Aortic arches">Aortic arches</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erytrocyte_deoxy_to_oxy_v0.7.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="320" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Erytrocyte_deoxy_to_oxy_v0.7.gif/220px-Erytrocyte_deoxy_to_oxy_v0.7.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Erytrocyte_deoxy_to_oxy_v0.7.gif 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Erytrocyte_deoxy_to_oxy_v0.7.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Animation of a typical human red blood cell cycle in the circulatory system. This animation occurs at a faster rate (~20 seconds of the average <a href="/wiki/Red_blood_cell#Human" title="Red blood cell">60-second cycle</a>) and shows the red blood cell deforming as it enters capillaries, as well as the bars changing color as the cell alternates in states of oxygenation along the circulatory system.</div></div></div>
<p>The human arterial system originates from the <a href="/wiki/Aortic_arches" title="Aortic arches">aortic arches</a> and from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dorsal_aortae" title="Dorsal aortae">dorsal aortae</a> starting from week 4 of embryonic life. The first and second aortic arches regress and form only the <a href="/wiki/Maxillary_artery" title="Maxillary artery">maxillary arteries</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stapedial_artery" title="Stapedial artery">stapedial arteries</a> respectively. The arterial system itself arises from aortic arches 3, 4 and 6 (aortic arch 5 completely regresses).
</p><p>The dorsal aortae, present on the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dorsal" title="wikt:dorsal">dorsal</a> side of the embryo, are initially present on both sides of the embryo. They later fuse to form the basis for the <a href="/wiki/Aorta" title="Aorta">aorta</a> itself. Approximately thirty smaller arteries branch from this at the back and sides. These branches form the <a href="/wiki/Intercostal_arteries" title="Intercostal arteries">intercostal arteries</a>, arteries of the arms and legs, lumbar arteries and the lateral sacral arteries. Branches to the sides of the aorta will form the definitive <a href="/wiki/Renal_artery" title="Renal artery">renal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inferior_suprarenal_artery" title="Inferior suprarenal artery">suprarenal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gonadal_artery" title="Gonadal artery">gonadal arteries</a>. Finally, branches at the front of the aorta consist of the <a href="/wiki/Vitelline_arteries" title="Vitelline arteries">vitelline arteries</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umbilical_arteries" title="Umbilical arteries">umbilical arteries</a>. The vitelline arteries form the <a href="/wiki/Celiac_artery" title="Celiac artery">celiac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Superior_mesenteric_artery" title="Superior mesenteric artery">superior</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inferior_mesenteric_artery" title="Inferior mesenteric artery">inferior mesenteric arteries</a> of the gastrointestinal tract. After birth, the umbilical arteries will form the <a href="/wiki/Internal_iliac_artery" title="Internal iliac artery">internal iliac arteries</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Veins_2">Veins</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Vasculogenesis" title="Vasculogenesis">Vasculogenesis</a></div>
<p>The human venous system develops mainly from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vitelline_vein" title="Vitelline vein">vitelline veins</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Umbilical_vein" title="Umbilical vein">umbilical veins</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Posterior_cardinal_vein" title="Posterior cardinal vein">cardinal veins</a>, all of which empty into the <a href="/wiki/Sinus_venosus" title="Sinus venosus">sinus venosus</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Function">Function</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Blood#Oxygen_transport" title="Blood">Blood § Oxygen transport</a></div>
<p>About 98.5% of the <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> in a sample of <a href="/wiki/Arterial_blood" title="Arterial blood">arterial blood</a> in a healthy human, breathing air at sea-level pressure, is chemically combined with <a href="/wiki/Hemoglobin" title="Hemoglobin">hemoglobin</a> molecules. About 1.5% is physically dissolved in the other blood liquids and not connected to hemoglobin. The hemoglobin molecule is the primary transporter of oxygen in vertebrates.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Clinical_significance">Clinical significance</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_circulatory_system_conditions" title="List of circulatory system conditions">List of circulatory system conditions</a></div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Health_and_disease"></span>
Many diseases affect the circulatory system. These include a number of <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular diseases</a>, affecting the heart and blood vessels; <a href="/wiki/Hematologic_disease" title="Hematologic disease">hematologic diseases</a> that affect the blood, such as <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">anemia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_disease" title="Lymphatic disease">lymphatic diseases</a> affecting the lymphatic system. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiologist" title="Cardiologist">Cardiologists</a> are medical professionals which specialise in the heart, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiothoracic_surgeon" title="Cardiothoracic surgeon">cardiothoracic surgeons</a> specialise in operating on the heart and its surrounding areas. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vascular_surgeon" title="Vascular surgeon">Vascular surgeons</a> focus on the blood vessels.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardiovascular_disease">Cardiovascular disease</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">Cardiovascular disease</a></div>
<p>Diseases affecting the cardiovascular system are called <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular disease</a>.
</p><p>Many of these diseases are called "<a href="/wiki/Lifestyle_disease" title="Lifestyle disease">lifestyle diseases</a>" because they develop over time and are related to a person's exercise habits, diet, whether they smoke, and other lifestyle choices a person makes. <a href="/wiki/Atherosclerosis" title="Atherosclerosis">Atherosclerosis</a> is the precursor to many of these diseases. It is where small <a href="/wiki/Atheroma" title="Atheroma">atheromatous plaques</a> build up in the walls of medium and large arteries. This may eventually grow or rupture to occlude the arteries. It is also a risk factor for <a href="/wiki/Acute_coronary_syndrome" title="Acute coronary syndrome">acute coronary syndromes</a>, which are diseases that are characterised by a sudden deficit of oxygenated blood to the heart tissue. Atherosclerosis is also associated with problems such as <a href="/wiki/Aneurysm" title="Aneurysm">aneurysm</a> formation or splitting ("dissection") of arteries.
</p><p>Another major cardiovascular disease involves the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Thrombus" title="Thrombus">clot, called a "thrombus"</a>. These can originate in veins or arteries. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_venous_thrombosis" title="Deep venous thrombosis">Deep venous thrombosis</a>, which mostly occurs in the legs, is one cause of clots in the veins of the legs, particularly when a person has been stationary for a long time. These clots may <a href="/wiki/Embolus" title="Embolus">embolise</a>, meaning travel to another location in the body. The results of this may include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulmonary_embolus" title="Pulmonary embolus">pulmonary embolus</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transient_ischaemic_attack" title="Transient ischaemic attack">transient ischaemic attacks</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a>.
</p><p>Cardiovascular diseases may also be congenital in nature, such as <a href="/wiki/Congenital_heart_defect" title="Congenital heart defect">heart defects</a> or <a href="/wiki/Persistent_fetal_circulation" title="Persistent fetal circulation">persistent fetal circulation</a>, where the circulatory changes that are supposed to happen after birth do not. Not all congenital changes to the circulatory system are associated with diseases, a large number are <a href="/wiki/Anatomical_variation" title="Anatomical variation">anatomical variations</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Investigations">Investigations</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="746" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif/220px-Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif/330px-Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif/440px-Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arteria-lusoria_MRA_MIP.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_angiography" title="Magnetic resonance angiography">Magnetic resonance angiography</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aberrant_subclavian_artery" title="Aberrant subclavian artery">aberrant subclavian artery</a></div></div></div>
<p>The function and health of the circulatory system and its parts are measured in a variety of manual and automated ways. These include simple methods such as those that are part of the <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_examination" title="Cardiovascular examination">cardiovascular examination</a>, including the taking of a person's <a href="/wiki/Pulse" title="Pulse">pulse</a> as an indicator of a person's <a href="/wiki/Heart_rate" title="Heart rate">heart rate</a>, the taking of <a href="/wiki/Blood_pressure" title="Blood pressure">blood pressure</a> through a <a href="/wiki/Sphygmomanometer" title="Sphygmomanometer">sphygmomanometer</a> or the use of a <a href="/wiki/Stethoscope" title="Stethoscope">stethoscope</a> to listen to the heart for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardiac_murmur" title="Cardiac murmur">murmurs</a> which may indicate problems with the <a href="/wiki/Heart_valve" title="Heart valve">heart's valves</a>. An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrocardiogram" title="Electrocardiogram">electrocardiogram</a> can also be used to evaluate the way in which electricity is conducted through the heart.
</p><p>Other more invasive means can also be used. A <a href="/wiki/Cannula" title="Cannula">cannula</a> or <a href="/wiki/Catheter" title="Catheter">catheter</a> inserted into an artery may be used to measure <a href="/wiki/Pulse_pressure" title="Pulse pressure">pulse pressure</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_wedge_pressure" title="Pulmonary wedge pressure">pulmonary wedge pressures</a>. Angiography, which involves injecting a dye into an artery to visualise an arterial tree, can be used in the heart (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coronary_angiography" title="Coronary angiography">coronary angiography</a>) or brain. At the same time as the arteries are visualised, blockages or narrowings may be fixed through the insertion of <a href="/wiki/Stent" title="Stent">stents</a>, and active bleeds may be managed by the insertion of coils. An MRI may be used to image arteries, called an <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_angiography" title="Magnetic resonance angiography">MRI angiogram</a>. For evaluation of the blood supply to the lungs a <a href="/wiki/CT_pulmonary_angiogram" title="CT pulmonary angiogram">CT pulmonary angiogram</a> may be used. <a href="/wiki/Doppler_ultrasonography#Blood_vessels" title="Doppler ultrasonography">Vascular ultrasonography</a> may be used to investigate <a href="/wiki/Vascular_disease" title="Vascular disease">vascular diseases</a> affecting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venous_system" title="Venous system">venous system</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arterial_system" title="Arterial system">arterial system</a> including the diagnosis of <a href="/wiki/Stenosis" title="Stenosis">stenosis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultrasonography_of_deep_venous_thrombosis" title="Ultrasonography of deep venous thrombosis">thrombosis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ultrasonography_of_chronic_venous_insufficiency_of_the_legs" title="Ultrasonography of chronic venous insufficiency of the legs">venous insufficiency</a>. An <a href="/wiki/Intravascular_ultrasound" title="Intravascular ultrasound">intravascular ultrasound</a> using a <a href="/wiki/Catheter" title="Catheter">catheter</a> is also an option.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surgery">Surgery</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left
